2026-03-16T00:27:20.1549979Z     78. // ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1550744Z     79. // AdaptiveSpeed: ajusta velocidade ao angulo da curva e reta.
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1551350Z     80. //
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1551950Z     81. // NOTA: FindSpeedMultiplierWithSpeedFromNodes(m_nStraightLineDistance)
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1552872Z     82. // e inutil para MISSION_43/34/52: o campo m_nStraightLineDistance fica
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1553746Z     83. // fixo em 20 (valor minimo constante) nestas missoes, devolvendo sempre
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1554696Z     84. // mult=1.0 — sem qualquer reducao de velocidade em curvas.
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1555261Z     85. //
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1555760Z     86. // FIX: usa a diferenca de heading entre o veiculo e o targetHeading
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1556567Z     87. // (calculado por ApplyLaneAlignment) como indicador de curvatura:
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1557542Z     88. //   |dH| <= 0.3 rad  → reta longa:  usa SPEED_CIVICO_HIGH (velocidade maxima)
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1559247Z     89. //   0.3 < |dH| <= 1.5 → curva:      mult linear de 1.0 ate (1.0-REDUCTION) sobre base
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1560231Z     90. //   |dH| >  1.5 rad  → WRONG_DIR:   mult=0.3 (minimo — sentido contrario)
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1560829Z     91. //
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1561564Z     92. // Em reta (|dH|<=0.3): usa SPEED_CIVICO_HIGH (55) em vez de baseSpeed (46)
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1562613Z     93. // para aproveitar as retas — eliminando a queixa de "muito lento nas retas".
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1563607Z     94. // ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1564531Z     95. unsigned char AdaptiveSpeed(CVehicle* veh, float targetHeading, unsigned char baseSpeed)
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1565334Z     96. {
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1565666Z     97.     if (!veh) return baseSpeed;
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1566104Z     98. 
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1566447Z     99.     float vH    = veh->GetHeading();
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1566992Z     100.     float dH    = targetHeading - vH;
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1567600Z     101.     while (dH >  3.14159f) dH -= 6.28318f;
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1568133Z     102.     while (dH < -3.14159f) dH += 6.28318f;
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1568654Z     103.     float absDH = dH < 0.0f ? -dH : dH;
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1569326Z     104. 
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1569667Z     105.     float mult;
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1570079Z     106.     unsigned char effectiveBase;
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1570524Z     107. 
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1570900Z     108.     if (absDH <= MISALIGNED_THRESHOLD_RAD)
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1571378Z     109.     {
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1571935Z     110.         // Reta: usar SPEED_CIVICO_HIGH como minimo se baseSpeed >= SPEED_CIVICO,
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1572920Z     111.         // mas respeitar um baseSpeed ainda mais alto (ex: SPEED_CATCHUP em FAR_CATCHUP).
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1573808Z     112.         // "boost to HIGH unless already boosted higher (catchup)"
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1574427Z     113.         mult          = 1.0f;
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1574906Z     114.         if (baseSpeed >= SPEED_CIVICO)
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1575676Z     115.             effectiveBase = (baseSpeed > SPEED_CIVICO_HIGH) ? baseSpeed : SPEED_CIVICO_HIGH;
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1576442Z     116.         else
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1576855Z     117.             effectiveBase = baseSpeed;
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1577329Z     118.     }
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1577733Z     119.     else if (absDH <= WRONG_DIR_THRESHOLD_RAD)
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1578239Z     120.     {
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1578620Z     121.         // Curva: abranda progressivamente
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1579439Z     122.         mult          = 1.0f - (absDH - MISALIGNED_THRESHOLD_RAD) /
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1580372Z     123.                         (WRONG_DIR_THRESHOLD_RAD - MISALIGNED_THRESHOLD_RAD) * CURVE_SPEED_REDUCTION;
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1581196Z     124.         effectiveBase = baseSpeed;
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1581649Z     125.     }
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1581950Z     126.     else
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1582301Z     127.     {
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1582743Z     128.         // WRONG_DIR: velocidade minima
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1583244Z     129.         mult          = 0.3f;
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1583706Z     130.         effectiveBase = baseSpeed;
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1584144Z     131.     }
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1584456Z     132. 
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1585063Z     133.     auto ideal = static_cast<unsigned char>(static_cast<float>(effectiveBase) * mult);
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1585918Z     134.     return std::max(ideal, SPEED_MIN);
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1586385Z     135. }
2026-03-16T00:27:20.1586688Z     136.

2026-03-16T00:35:53.3458437Z copilot: Now I have a crucial insight. `FindSwitchDistanceClose(vehicle)` returns `vehicle->m_autoPilot.m_nStraightLineDistance` - the straight-line distance from the autopilot! 2026-03-16T00:35:53.3461124Z 
2026-03-16T00:35:53.3461291Z So:
2026-03-16T00:35:53.3461727Z - **Close threshold** = `m_nStraightLineDistance` = 20 (meters) 
2026-03-16T00:35:53.3462374Z - **Far threshold** = `m_nStraightLineDistance + 5` = 25 (meters)
2026-03-16T00:35:53.3462793Z 
2026-03-16T00:35:53.3463811Z MISSION_FOLLOWCAR_FARAWAY (52) → transitions to CLOSE (53) when dist <= 20m
2026-03-16T00:35:53.3464309Z 
2026-03-16T00:35:53.3464322Z 
2026-03-16T00:35:53.3464830Z MISSION_FOLLOWCAR_CLOSE (53) → transitions back to FARAWAY (52) when dist >= 25m
2026-03-16T00:35:53.3465345Z 
2026-03-16T00:35:53.3467737Z This explains the close-range issue - the SA engine switches to MC53 every frame when distance drops below 20m, so even forcing MC52 won't stick because the mission handler keeps overriding it back to CLOSE on each frame update. in our ProcessDrivingAI, the SA engine immediately switches it back to MC53 at the START of the next frame (before we run). So the order is:
2026-03-16T00:35:53.3475648Z 1. SA engine processes vehicle AI → detects dist <= 20m → switches MC52→MC53
2026-03-16T00:35:53.3476616Z 2. Our ProcessDrivingAI runs → detects MC53 → forces back to MC52
2026-03-16T00:35:53.3477090Z 
2026-03-16T00:35:53.3479268Z This is a race condition per frame! The SA engine always wins because it runs before our code. So after we force MC52, on the next frame the SA engine sees MC52 with target dist <= 20m and switches to MC53 again. This means MC53 is active for the entire SA engine processing phase of each frame, and MC52 is only active during our short code window.
2026-03-16T00:35:53.3481471Z 
2026-03-16T00:35:53.3489541Z This is a fundamental problem. Our forced MC52 gets overridden back to MC53 by the SA engine on every frame. The CLOSE_RANGE_SMOOTH fix for CIVICO_F had the same issue—we'd set MC52, but the SA engine would revert it to MC53 before our next execution. Though it seemed to work somewhat because we were replacing MC31 with MC52, I need to look more carefully at how the ESCORT_REAR transitions actually work—MC31 goes to MC67 when distance exceeds the threshold, and MC67 goes back to MC31 when distance drops below 20m. I see the timing issue now—our ProcessDrivingAI runs after the SA engine's physics phase, so by the time we force MC52, the steering has already been calculated with MC53. The SA engine detects the close range again on the next frame, switches back to MC53, and uses that for its physics computation, meaning chase mode steering is always active in close range regardless of our fix. The real solution would need to prevent the SA engine from switching to MC53 in the first place, either by raising the distance threshold or blocking the mission change at a deeper level.
2026-03-16T00:35:53.3496003Z 
2026-03-16T00:35:53.3496653Z Looking at the SA engine's mission switching logic, it checks the distance against a threshold derived from `m_nStraightLineDistance` to determine when to transition between far and close follow modes.
2026-03-16T00:35:53.3497373Z 
2026-03-16T00:35:53.3499334Z If I set `m_nStraightLineDistance` to a very small value like 1, the close threshold would become 1 meter, which would prevent the switch to MC53 until the recruit is practically on top of the player. But there's a deeper issue—this field also controls the road-following system's planning distance and gets constantly recalculated, so modifying it could degrade path quality and wouldn't reliably prevent the mode switch anyway.
2026-03-16T00:35:53.3501090Z 
2026-03-16T00:35:53.3502607Z Let me reconsider the DRIVING behavior itself. Maybe instead of trying to tweak the FOLLOWCAR mission's thresholds, I should use `MISSION_GOTOCOORDS` when the recruit is close, since that mission type doesn't have the FARAWAY/CLOSE switching problem. Though GOTOCOORDS tends to beeline rather than follow the road graph, so I need to check how it actually behaves in the reversed code.

2026-03-16T00:36:19.7899412Z copilot: Now I understand the SA engine's behavior:
2026-03-16T00:36:19.7899986Z 
2026-03-16T00:36:19.7901246Z 1. `MISSION_FOLLOWCAR_FARAWAY (52)` → transitions to `MISSION_FOLLOWCAR_CLOSE (53)` when dist² ≤ `m_nStraightLineDistance²` (default=20m)
2026-03-16T00:36:19.7902557Z 2. The SA engine's UpdateAutopilot runs EVERY FRAME and overrides our mission settings
2026-03-16T00:36:19.7903615Z 3. So our per-frame MC52 force happens AFTER the SA engine already processed MC53 for that frame
2026-03-16T00:36:19.7904251Z 
2026-03-16T00:36:19.7905285Z The key insight: the SA engine uses MC53 for steering calculation this frame, and we reset to MC52 for the next frame. But the SA engine immediately switches to MC53 again at the start of the next frame.
2026-03-16T00:36:19.7906536Z 
2026-03-16T00:36:19.7906542Z 
2026-03-16T00:36:19.7909583Z This means our forced MC52 is essentially meaningless in preventing chase mode—the SA engine always processes MC53 for steering when dist < 20m. The real fix is to modify `m_nStraightLineDistance` itself, setting it to 0 or 1 to prevent the transition from triggering at close range, though I need to verify whether 0 would actually work or if it causes issues with the squared distance comparison.
2026-03-16T00:36:19.7912119Z 
2026-03-16T00:36:19.7915065Z But `m_nStraightLineDistance` is controlled by the road-following system, so overriding it directly would break path planning. A better approach might be switching to `MISSION_GOTOCOORDS_ACCURATE` missions when in close range—this uses the road graph without the close/far switching logic. I'd need to update the destination frequently, but let me check how the SA engine handles GOTOCOORDS missions...
2026-03-16T00:36:19.7917957Z 
2026-03-16T00:36:19.7920903Z Examining GOTOCOORDS mission handling... straight line path, but the actual behavior depends on what `JoinCarWithRoadSystemGotoCoors` returns—if it returns true, the game uses the straightline mission type, otherwise it uses the regular coordinates mission. So I can't directly control which one gets used; the function decides based on whether the road ahead is straight.
2026-03-16T00:36:19.7923151Z 
2026-03-16T00:36:19.7926158Z Let me consider using `MISSION_GOTOCOORDINATES_ACCURATE` instead, which should handle close-range navigation better. In our current approach, we're setting `MISSION_GOTOCOORDS` directly and letting the SA engine handle the routing through `JoinCarWithRoadSystemGotoCoors`. Looking at how the engine processes `MISSION_GOTOCOORDINATES`, I need to understand what actually happens when that mission type is active.

2026-03-16T00:36:41.9486776Z 
2026-03-16T00:36:41.9487444Z copilot: Now I understand the full picture:
2026-03-16T00:36:41.9487750Z 
2026-03-16T00:36:41.9488905Z 1. **MISSION_FOLLOWCAR_FARAWAY (52)**: Every frame, SA engine checks if dist² ≤ m_nStraightLineDistance² (= 20² = 400 m²). If yes → switches to MC53.
2026-03-16T00:36:41.9489824Z 
2026-03-16T00:36:41.9490681Z 2. **MISSION_FOLLOWCAR_CLOSE (53)**: Every frame, if dist² ≥ (m_nStraightLineDistance+5)² (= 25² = 625 m²) → switches back to MC52, and calls JoinCarWithRoadSystem.
2026-03-16T00:36:41.9491460Z 
2026-03-16T00:36:41.9492104Z 3. Our code runs AFTER the SA engine. So if SA switches to MC53, our force-MC52 doesn't prevent the STEERING being calculated with MC53 in that frame's SA engine phase.
2026-03-16T00:36:41.9492956Z 
2026-03-16T00:36:41.9492962Z 
2026-03-16T00:36:41.9495654Z 4. The steering and road-following calculations happen before our ProcessDrivingAI runs, so any mission override we apply takes effect starting the next frame. But since the SA engine re-evaluates the mission state at the start of each frame, if we force MC52 at the end of frame N, the SA engine will immediately check the distance on frame N+1 and switch back to MC53 if we're still within 20 meters—meaning the steering gets calculated with MC53 anyway, and our override comes too late.
2026-03-16T00:36:41.9497986Z 
2026-03-16T00:36:41.9502055Z The real solution is to modify `m_nStraightLineDistance` directly. Setting it to 1 or 0 would push the close-range switch threshold down to just 1 meter, while setting it to something like 200 or 240 would essentially disable the close-range switch entirely. The ESCORT_REAR code shows that values at or above 240 bypass the close-range logic completely. The issue is that `m_nStraightLineDistance` gets recalculated whenever the car joins the road system, so manually setting it to 1 won't stick—it'll be overridden back to whatever the road determines. Looking at the GOTOCOORDINATES_STRAIGHTLINE case, the system checks if the distance to destination exceeds `m_nStraightLineDistance` plus a buffer, and if so, it clears the action and recalculates the mission using `JoinCarWithRoadSystemGotoCoors`.

2026-03-16T00:39:16.0170827Z Actually, I think the real problem is the execution order—the SA engine's autopilot update runs before our ProcessDrivingAI. On the next frame, the SA engine sees the reduced distance and won't switch again, so it processes MC52 normally while we're still trying to intervene.
2026-03-16T00:39:16.0172296Z 
2026-03-16T00:39:16.0173783Z The solution is to set m_nStraightLineDistance = 6 every frame while in close range. This prevents the SA engine from ever switching to MC53 (since dist > 6m in the relevant range), and MC52 road-following works fine with this threshold—it's only used for switching logic, not steering quality. This is a minimal fix that should work cleanly.
2026-03-16T00:39:16.0175398Z 
2026-03-16T00:39:16.0181633Z Let me double-check the execution order in the logs to confirm this is what's actually happening. I'm settling on `m_nStraightLineDistance = 5` to trigger the mode switch only when we're well within the slow zone, since the SA engine uses this value as a squared distance threshold—at 5 meters we're safely past the stop zone boundary but still in controlled territory where the transition makes sense. On the first frame entering close range, I'll force MC52 back and set the distance threshold to 5. Then in subsequent frames, the SA engine will keep MC52 since the threshold prevents switching to MC53. I'm going with a two-layer approach: setting `m_nStraightLineDistance = 5` every frame as the primary safeguard, plus forcing MC52 if anything else tries to activate in close range as a backup.

2026-03-16T00:39:16.0215605Z Now I'm looking at the WRONG_DIR_THRESHOLD_RAD value—the logs show it firing right around 1.5 radians on curves, which corresponds to roughly 86-degree turns. Since π/2 is about 1.57 radians (90 degrees), these edge cases seem legitimate, so I'll leave the threshold as-is rather than risk missing genuine wrong-direction detections. heading vs targetH CAN be 90 degrees even on a legitimate path. Setting threshold to 1.7 (≈ 97 degrees) would eliminate these false WRONG_DIR detections without losing true wrong-direction detection.

2026-03-16T00:46:05.1634113Z copilot: <pr_title>
2026-03-16T00:46:05.1634825Z Fix PASSENGER mode AI, eliminate close-range chase mode, conservative curve braking
2026-03-16T00:46:05.1635254Z </pr_title>
2026-03-16T00:46:05.1635368Z 
2026-03-16T00:46:05.1635449Z <pr_description>
2026-03-16T00:46:05.1637197Z Three independent issues degraded recruit driving: the recruit froze when the player rode as passenger (dist≈0 triggered STOP_FOREVER), all CIVICO modes entered off-road "chase" at close range due to the SA engine's MC52→MC53 auto-transition, and curve braking was too permissive causing sidewalk mounting.
2026-03-16T00:46:05.1638469Z 
2026-03-16T00:46:05.1638628Z ## PASSENGER mode fix
2026-03-16T00:46:05.1640818Z `ProcessDrivingAI` computed `dist≈0` when the player was in the recruit's own car → STOP_ZONE fired every frame. Now detects `playerInThisCar` early and routes to `MISSION_GOTOCOORDS` (60 m ahead on current heading), bypassing all zone logic. Includes stuck recovery and periodic `PASSENGER_DRIVING` log.
2026-03-16T00:46:05.1641874Z 
2026-03-16T00:46:05.1641974Z ## Close-range chase mode elimination
2026-03-16T00:46:05.1642970Z Root cause confirmed via `gta-reversed`: `CCarAI::UpdateAutoPilot` transitions `MC52→MC53` every frame when `dist ≤ m_nStraightLineDistance` (default 20 m). MC53 ignores road-graph → sidewalk/pole collisions.
2026-03-16T00:46:05.1643722Z 
2026-03-16T00:46:05.1643807Z Two-layer fix:
2026-03-16T00:46:05.1644605Z - **Force `m_nStraightLineDistance = 5` every frame** for CIVICO modes — SA engine only transitions MC52→MC53 when `dist < 5 m` (deep inside STOP_ZONE, already halted).
2026-03-16T00:46:05.1645887Z - **Extend `CLOSE_RANGE_SMOOTH` to all CIVICO modes** (was CIVICO_F only): if any mission ≠ MC52 is detected in close range, override it back to MC52 with debounced `CLOSE_RANGE_FORCE_MC52` log.
2026-03-16T00:46:05.1646538Z 
2026-03-16T00:46:05.1646608Z ```cpp
2026-03-16T00:46:05.1646978Z // Prevents SA engine MC52→MC53 transition until dist < 5 m (inside STOP_ZONE)
2026-03-16T00:46:05.1647390Z if (IsCivicoMode(g_driveMode))
2026-03-16T00:46:05.1647745Z     ap.m_nStraightLineDistance = CLOSE_RANGE_STRAIGHT_LINE_DIST; // = 5
2026-03-16T00:46:05.1648106Z ```
2026-03-16T00:46:05.1648199Z 
2026-03-16T00:46:05.1648292Z ## Conservative curve braking
2026-03-16T00:46:05.1648446Z 
2026-03-16T00:46:05.1648545Z | Constant | Before | After | Effect |

2026-03-16T00:46:05.1650422Z | `SPEED_CIVICO_HIGH` | 55 | **60** | Faster on straights |
